He said: and Iblis, may God curse him, will stand and say: {And I had no authority over you except that I called you and you responded to me}, the verse.

Then, having mentioned the fate of the wretched and what they came to of disgrace and retribution, and that their orator was Iblis, God Most High turns to the state of the blessed, and that they will enter, on the Day of Resurrection, gardens beneath which rivers flow, roaming freely within them wherever they go and wherever they wander, {abiding therein} forever, remaining there eternally, never being moved or removed, {by the permission of their Lord; their greeting therein is peace}, as God Most High said: {Until, when they reach it and its gates are opened, its keepers say to them: Peace be upon you} [al-Zumar: 73], and God Most High said: {And the angels enter upon them from every gate: Peace be upon you} [al-Ra'd: 23-24], and God Most High said: {And they will be met therein with greeting and peace} [al-Furqan: 75], and He said: {Their call therein will be: Glory be to You, O God, and their greeting therein will be: Peace, and the end of their call will be: Praise be to God, Lord of the worlds} [Yunus: 10].

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى عَمَّا خَطَبَ بِهِ إِبْلِيسُ [لَعَنَهُ اللَّهُ] أَتْبَاعَهُ، بَعْدَمَا قَضَى اللَّهُ بَيْنَ عِبَادِهِ، فَأَدْخَلَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ الْجَنَّاتِ، وَأَسْكَنَ الْكَافِرِينَ الدَّرَكَاتِ، فَقَامَ فِيهِمْ إِبْلِيسُ -لَعَنَهُ اللَّهُ -حِينَئِذٍ خَطِيبًا لِيَزِيدَهُمْ حُزْنًا إِلَى حُزْنِهِمْ وغَبنا إِلَى غبْنهم، وَحَسْرَةً إِلَى حَسْرَتِهِمْ، فَقَالَ: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَعَدَكُمْ وَعْدَ الْحَقِّ﴾ أَيْ: عَلَى أَلْسِنَةِ رُسُلِهِ، وَوَعَدَكُمْ فِي اتِّبَاعِهِمُ النَّجَاةَ وَالسَّلَامَةَ، وَكَانَ وَعْدًا حَقًّا، وَخَبَرًا صِدْقًا، وَأَمَّا أَنَا فَوَعَدْتُكُمْ وَأَخْلَفْتُكُمْ، كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿يَعِدُهُمْ وَيُمَنِّيهِمْ وَمَا يَعِدُهُمُ الشَّيْطَانُ إِلا غُرُورًا﴾ [النِّسَاءِ: ١٢٠] .

ثُمَّ قَالَ: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لِي عَلَيْكُمْ مِنْ سُلْطَانٍ﴾ أَيْ: مَا كَانَ لِيَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِيمَا دَعَوْتُكُمْ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ دَلِيلٍ وَلَا حُجَّةٍ عَلَى صِدْقٍ مَا وَعَدْتُكُمْ بِهِ، ﴿إِلا أَنْ دَعَوْتُكُمْ فَاسْتَجَبْتُمْ لِي﴾ بِمُجَرَّدِ ذَلِكَ، هَذَا وَقَدْ أَقَامَتْ عَلَيْكُمُ الرُّسُلُ الْحُجَجَ وَالْأَدِلَّةَ الصَّحِيحَةَ عَلَى صِدْقِ مَا جَاءُوكُمْ بِهِ، فَخَالَفْتُمُوهُمْ فَصِرْتُمْ إِلَى مَا أَنْتُمْ فِيهِ، ﴿فَلا تَلُومُونِي﴾ الْيَوْمَ، ﴿وَلُومُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ﴾ فَإِنَّ الذَّنْبَ لَكُمْ، لِكَوْنِكُمْ خَالَفْتُمُ الْحُجَجَ وَاتَّبَعْتُمُونِي بِمُجَرَّدِ مَا دَعَوْتُكُمْ إِلَى الْبَاطِلِ، ﴿مَا أَنَا بِمُصْرِخِكُمْ﴾ أَيْ: بِنَافِعِكُمْ وَمُنْقِذِكُمْ وَمُخَلِّصِكُمْ مِمَّا أَنْتُمْ فِيهِ، ﴿وَمَا أَنْتُمْ بِمُصْرِخِيَّ﴾ أَيْ: بِنَافِعِيَّ بِإِنْقَاذِي مِمَّا أَنَا فِيهِ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ وَالنَّكَالِ، ﴿إِنِّي كَفَرْتُ بِمَا أَشْرَكْتُمُونِ مِنْ قَبْلُ﴾

قَالَ قَتَادَةُ: أَيْ بِسَبَبِ مَا أَشْرَكْتُمُونِ مِنْ قَبْلُ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: يَقُولُ: إِنِّي جَحَدْتُ أَنْ أَكُونَ شَرِيكًا لله، عز وجل.

وهذا الذي قال هُوَ الرَّاجِحُ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنْ يَدْعُو مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ مَنْ لَا يَسْتَجِيبُ لَهُ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَهُمْ عَنْ دُعَائِهِمْ غَافِلُونَ وَإِذَا حُشِرَ النَّاسُ كَانُوا لَهُمْ أَعْدَاءً وَكَانُوا بِعِبَادَتِهِمْ كَافِرِينَ﴾ [الْأَحْقَافِ: ٥، ٦] ، وَقَالَ: ﴿كَلا سَيَكْفُرُونَ بِعِبَادَتِهِمْ وَيَكُونُونَ عَلَيْهِمْ ضِدًّا﴾ [مَرْيَمَ: ٨٢] .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿إِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ﴾ أَيْ: فِي إِعْرَاضِهِمْ عَنِ الْحَقِّ وَاتِّبَاعِهِمُ الْبَاطِلَ ﴿لَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌ﴾

وَالظَّاهِرُ مِنْ سِيَاقِ الْآيَةِ: أَنَّ هَذِهِ الْخُطْبَةَ تَكُونُ مِنْ إِبْلِيسَ بَعْدَ دُخُولِهِمُ النَّارَ، كَمَا قَدَّمْنَا. وَلَكِنْ قَدْ وَرَدَ فِي حَدِيثٍ رَوَاهُ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ -وَهَذَا لَفْظُهُ -وَابْنُ جَرِيرٍ مِنْ رِوَايَةِ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ زِيَادٍ: حَدَّثَنِي دُخَيْنٌ الحَجْري، عَنْ عُقْبَةَ بْنِ عَامِرٍ، عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: "إِذَا جَمَعَ اللَّهُ الْأَوَّلِينَ وَالْآخَرِينَ، فَقَضَى بَيْنَهُمْ، فَفَرَغَ مِنَ الْقَضَاءِ، قَالَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ: قَدْ قَضَى بَيْنَنَا رَبُّنَا، فَمَنْ يَشْفَعُ لَنَا؟ فَيَقُولُونَ: انْطَلِقُوا بِنَا إِلَى آدَمَ -وَذَكَرَ نُوحًا، وَإِبْرَاهِيمَ، وَمُوسَى، وَعِيسَى -فَيَقُولُ عِيسَى: أَدُلُّكُمْ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ الْأُمِّيِّ. فَيَأْتُونِي، فَيَأْذَنُ اللَّهُ لِي أَنْ أَقُومَ إِلَيْهِ فَيَثُورُ [مِنْ] مَجْلِسِي مِنْ أَطْيَبِ رِيحٍ شَمَّهَا أَحَدٌ قَطُّ، حَتَّى آتِيَ رَبِّي فَيُشَفِّعَنِي، وَيَجْعَلَ لِي نُورًا مِنْ شَعَرِ رَأْسِي إِلَى ظُفْرِ قَدَمِي، ثُمَّ يَقُولُ الْكَافِرُونَ هَذَا: قَدْ وَجَدَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ مَنْ يَشْفَعُ لَهُمْ، فَمَنْ يَشْفَعُ لَنَا؟ مَا هُوَ إِلَّا إِبْلِيسُ هُوَ الَّذِي أَضَلَّنَا، فَيَأْتُونَ إِبْلِيسَ فَيَقُولُونَ: قَدْ وَجَدَ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ مَنْ يَشْفَعُ لَهُمْ، فَقُمْ أَنْتَ فَاشْفَعْ لَنَا، فَإِنَّكَ أَنْتَ أَضْلَلْتَنَا. فَيَقُومُ فَيَثُورُ مِنْ مَجْلِسِهِ مِنْ أَنْتَنِ رِيحٍ شَمَّهَا أَحَدٌ قَطُّ، ثُمَّ يَعْظُمُ نَحِيبُهُمْ ﴿وَقَالَ الشَّيْطَانُ لَمَّا قُضِيَ الأمْرُ إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَعَدَكُمْ وَعْدَ الْحَقِّ وَوَعَدْتُكُمْ فَأَخْلَفْتُكُمْ وَمَا كَانَ لِي عَلَيْكُمْ مِنْ سُلْطَانٍ إِلا أَنْ دَعَوْتُكُمْ فَاسْتَجَبْتُمْ لِي فَلا تَلُومُونِي وَلُومُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ﴾ .

وَهَذَا سِيَاقُ ابْنِ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ، وَرَوَاهُ ابْنُ الْمُبَارَكِ عَنْ رِشْدين بْنِ سَعْدٍ، عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ زِيَادِ بْنِ أنْعُمٍ، عَنْ دُخَيْن عَنْ عُقْبَة، به مرفوعا .

وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ كَعْبٍ القُرظي، رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: لَمَّا قَالَ أَهْلُ النَّارِ: ﴿سَوَاءٌ عَلَيْنَا أَجَزِعْنَا أَمْ صَبَرْنَا مَا لَنَا مِنْ مَحِيصٍ﴾ قَالَ لَهُمْ إِبْلِيسُ: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَعَدَكُمْ وَعْدَ الْحَقِّ﴾ الْآيَةَ، فَلَمَّا سَمِعُوا مَقَالَتَهُ مَقَتُوا أَنْفُسَهُمْ، فَنُودُوا: ﴿لَمَقْتُ اللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ مِنْ مَقْتِكُمْ أَنْفُسَكُمْ إِذْ تُدْعَوْنَ إِلَى الإيمَانِ فَتَكْفُرُونَ﴾ [غَافِرٍ: ١٠] .

وَقَالَ عَامِرٌ الشَّعْبِيُّ: يَقُومُ خَطِيبَانِ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ عَلَى رُءُوسِ النَّاسِ، يَقُولُ اللَّهُ لِعِيسَى ابْنَ مَرْيَمَ: ﴿أَأَنْتَ قُلْتَ لِلنَّاسِ اتَّخِذُونِي وَأُمِّيَ إِلَهَيْنِ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ﴾ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ: ﴿قَالَ اللَّهُ هَذَا يَوْمُ يَنْفَعُ الصَّادِقِينَ صِدْقُهُمْ﴾ [الْمَائِدَةِ: ١١٦، ١١٩] ، قَالَ: وَيَقُومُ إِبْلِيسُ -لَعَنَهُ اللَّهُ -فَيَقُولُ: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لِي عَلَيْكُمْ مِنْ سُلْطَانٍ إِلا أَنْ دَعَوْتُكُمْ فَاسْتَجَبْتُمْ لِي﴾ الْآيَةَ.

ثُمَّ لَمَّا ذَكَرَ تَعَالَى مَآلَ الْأَشْقِيَاءِ وَمَا صَارُوا إِلَيْهِ مِنَ الْخِزْيِ والنَّكَال. وَأَنَّ خَطِيبَهُمْ إِبْلِيسُ، عَطَفَ بِحَالِ السُّعَدَاءِ وَأَنَّهُمْ يَدْخُلُونَ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ جَنَّاتٍ تَجْرِي مِنْ تَحْتِهَا الْأَنْهَارُ سَارِحَةً فِيهَا حَيْثُ سَارُوا وَأَيْنَ سَارُوا ﴿خَالِدِينَ فِيهَا﴾ مَاكِثِينَ أَبَدًا لَا يُحَوَّلُونَ وَلَا يَزُولُونَ، ﴿بِإِذْنِ رَبِّهِمْ تَحِيَّتُهُمْ فِيهَا سَلامٌ﴾ كَمَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿حَتَّى إِذَا جَاءُوهَا وَفُتِحَتْ أَبْوَابُهَا وَقَالَ لَهُمْ خَزَنَتُهَا سَلامٌ عَلَيْكُمْ﴾ [الزُّمَرِ: ٧٣] ، وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَالْمَلائِكَةُ يَدْخُلُونَ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ كُلِّ بَابٍ سَلامٌ عَلَيْكُمْ﴾ [الرَّعْدِ: ٢٣، ٢٤] وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَيُلَقَّوْنَ فِيهَا تَحِيَّةً وَسَلامًا﴾ [الْفُرْقَانِ: ٧٥] ، وَقَالَ: ﴿دَعْوَاهُمْ فِيهَا سُبْحَانَكَ اللَّهُمَّ وَتَحِيَّتُهُمْ فِيهَا سَلامٌ وَآخِرُ دَعْوَاهُمْ أَنِ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ﴾ [يُونُسَ: ١٠] .

---

## 14:24-26 — verses 24-26 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Ali ibn Abi Talhah said, on the authority of Ibn Abbas, regarding His saying {a good word, like a good tree}: it is the testimony that there is no god but Allah. {like a good tree}, that is the believer. {whose root is firm}, meaning: "there is no god but Allah" is firm in the heart of the believer. {and whose branch is in the sky}, meaning: the deeds of the believer are raised up to the sky by means of it.

Al-Dahhak, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, Ikrimah, Qatadah and others likewise said that this is an expression for the believer, his good speech, and his righteous deeds, and that the believer is like the palm tree, in that righteous deeds are continually raised up on his behalf at every time and moment, morning and evening.

Al-Suddi likewise related it, from Murrah, from Ibn Mas'ud, who said: it is the palm tree.

Shu'bah, from Mu'awiyah ibn Qurrah, from Anas: it is the palm tree.

Hammad ibn Salamah, from Shu'ayb ibn al-Habhab, from Anas: that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was brought a basket of fresh dates, and said, "{The likeness of a good word is like a good tree}," he said, "it is the palm tree."

This has been related from this route and others, from Anas as a mawquf (halted report), and Masruq, Mujahid, Ikrimah, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, al-Dahhak, Qatadah and others have stated the same explicitly.

Al-Bukhari said: Ubayd ibn Isma'il narrated to us, from Abu Usamah, from Ubaydullah, from Nafi', from Ibn Umar, who said: We were with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ when he said, "Tell me of a tree that resembles, or is like, the Muslim man: its leaves do not fall, [nor does it do such and such and such], and it gives its fruit at all times." Ibn Umar said: it occurred to me that it was the palm tree, but I saw Abu Bakr and Umar remaining silent, so I disliked to speak. When they said nothing, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "It is the palm tree." When we got up, I said to Umar: "O father, by Allah, it had occurred to me that it was the palm tree." He said: "What kept you from speaking?" I said: "I did not see you speaking, so I disliked to speak or say anything." Umar said: "Had you said it, that would have been dearer to me than such and such."

Ahmad said: Sufyan narrated to us, from Ibn Abi Najih, from Mujahid: I accompanied Ibn Umar to Madinah, and I did not hear him narrate anything from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ except one hadith. He said: We were with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and he was brought the pith of a palm tree, and he said, "Among the trees there is a tree whose likeness is that of the Muslim man." I wanted to say: it is the palm tree, but I looked and saw that I was the youngest of the people present, [so I kept silent]. Then the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "It is the palm tree." Both Bukhari and Muslim narrated it.

Malik and Abd al-Aziz said, from Abdullah ibn Dinar, from Ibn Umar, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said one day to his companions, "Among the trees there is a tree whose leaves do not fall, like the believer." He said: the people fell to naming trees of the desert, and it occurred to my heart that it was the palm tree, [but I felt too shy to speak, until the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "It is the palm tree]." Both Bukhari and Muslim narrated this as well.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: my father narrated to us, Musa ibn Isma'il narrated to us, Aban, that is Ibn Zayd al-Attar, narrated to us, Qatadah narrated to us: that a man said, "O Messenger of Allah, the people of wealth have taken away the rewards!" He said, "What do you think, if a man gathered up the goods of this world and piled them one upon another, would they reach the sky? Shall I not tell you of a deed whose root is in the earth and whose branch is in the sky?" He said, "What is it, O Messenger of Allah?" He said, "You say: there is no god but Allah, and Allah is greatest, and glory be to Allah, and praise be to Allah, ten times after every prayer. That is a deed whose root is in the earth and whose branch is in the sky."

And from Ibn Abbas, regarding {like a good tree}: he said, it is a tree in Paradise.

Regarding His saying {giving its fruit at all times}: it has been said, morning and evening. It has been said, every month. It has been said, every two months.

It has been said, every six months. It has been said, every seven months. It has been said, every year.

What is apparent from the context is that the believer's likeness is that of a tree from which fruit is continually found at every time, in summer or winter, night or day. Likewise the believer continually has righteous deeds raised up on his behalf during the hours of the night and the extremities of the day, at every time and moment.

{by permission of its Lord}, that is, complete, good, abundant, and wholesome. {And Allah presents examples for people so that they might remember}.

Regarding His saying {And the likeness of a bad word is like a bad tree}: this is the likeness of the disbelief of the disbeliever, having no root and no firmness. It is likened to the colocynth tree, which is also called "al-shiryan." [Shu'bah related it, from Mu'awiyah ibn Qurrah, from Anas ibn Malik: that it is the colocynth tree].

Abu Bakr al-Bazzar, the hafiz, said: Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn al-Sakan narrated to us, Abu Zayd Sa'id ibn al-Rabi' narrated to us, Shu'bah narrated to us, from Mu'awiyah ibn Qurrah, from Anas, I think he attributed it to the Prophet ﷺ, who said, "The likeness of a good word is like a good tree," he said, it is the palm tree. {And the likeness of a bad word is like a bad tree}, he said, it is al-shiryan.

He then related it from Muhammad ibn al-Muthanna, from Ghundar, from Shu'bah, from Mu'awiyah, from Anas, as a mawquf (halted report).

Ibn Abi Hatim said: my father narrated to us, Musa ibn Isma'il narrated to us, Hammad, that is Ibn Salamah, narrated to us, from Shu'ayb ibn al-Habhab, from Anas ibn Malik: that the Prophet ﷺ said, "{And the likeness of a bad word is like a bad tree}," it is the colocynth. I informed Abu al-Aliyah of that, and he said: this is what we used to hear.

Ibn Jarir related it from the hadith of Hammad ibn Salamah, with this wording. Abu Ya'la related it in his Musnad in fuller form than this, saying: Ghassan narrated to us, from Hammad, from Shu'ayb, from Anas: that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was brought a basket with fresh dates on it, and said, "The likeness of a good word is like a good tree, whose root is firm and whose branch is in the sky, giving its fruit at all times by permission of its Lord," and he said, "it is the palm tree." {And the likeness of a bad word is like a bad tree, uprooted from the surface of the earth, having no stability}, he said, "it is the colocynth." Shu'ayb said: I informed Abu al-Aliyah of that, and he said: that is what we used to hear.

Regarding His saying {uprooted}, that is, torn out entirely, {from the surface of the earth, having no stability}, meaning: it has no root and no firmness. Likewise disbelief has no root and no branch, and no deed of the disbeliever ascends, and nothing is accepted from him.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿مَثَلا كَلِمَةً طَيِّبَةً﴾ شَهَادَةُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، ﴿كَشَجَرَةٍ طَيِّبَةٍ﴾ وَهُوَ الْمُؤْمِنُ، ﴿أَصْلُهَا ثَابِتٌ﴾ يَقُولُ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ فِي قَلْبِ الْمُؤْمِنِ، ﴿وَفَرْعُهَا فِي السَّمَاءِ﴾ يَقُولُ: يُرْفَعُ بِهَا عَمَلُ الْمُؤْمِنِ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ.

وَهَكَذَا قَالَ الضَّحَّاكُ، وَسَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَير، وعِكْرِمة وَقَتَادَةُ وَغَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ: إِنَّ ذَلِكَ عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِ، وَقَوْلِهِ الطَّيِّبِ، وَعَمَلِهِ الصَّالِحِ، وَإِنَّ الْمُؤْمِنَ كَالشَّجَرَةِ مِنَ النَّخْلِ، لَا يَزَالُ يُرْفَعُ لَهُ عَمَلٌ صَالِحٌ فِي كُلِّ حِينٍ وَوَقْتٍ، وَصَبَاحٍ وَمَسَاءٍ.

وَهَكَذَا رَوَاهُ السُّدِّي، عَنْ مُرَّة، عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ.

وَشُعْبَةُ، عَنْ مُعَاوِيَةَ بْنِ قُرَة، عَنْ أَنَسٍ: هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ.

وَحَمَّادُ بْنُ سَلَمَةَ، عَنْ شُعَيْبِ بْنِ الْحَبْحَابِ، عَنْ أَنَسٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَتَى بِقِنَاعِ بُسْر فَقَالَ: "وَمَثَلُ كَلِمَةٍ طَيِّبَةٍ كَشَجَرَةٍ طَيِّبَةٍ" قَالَ: "هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ" .

وَرُوِيَ مِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ وَمِنْ غَيْرِهِ، عَنْ أَنَسٍ مَوْقُوفًا وَكَذَا نَصَّ عَلَيْهِ مَسْرُوقٌ، وَمُجَاهِدٌ، وَعِكْرِمَةُ، وَسَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ، وَالضَّحَّاكُ، وَقَتَادَةُ وَغَيْرُهُمْ.

وَقَالَ الْبُخَارِيُّ: حَدَّثَنَا عُبَيدُ بْنُ إِسْمَاعِيلَ، عَنْ أَبِي أُسَامَةَ، عَنْ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنْ نَافِعٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: كُنَّا عِنْدَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَقَالَ: "أَخْبِرُونِي عَنْ شَجَرَةٍ تُشْبِهُ -أَوْ: كَالرَّجُلِ -اَلْمُسْلِمِ، لَا يَتَحَاتُّ وَرَقُهَا [وَلَا وَلَا وَلَا] تُؤْتِي أُكُلَهَا كُلَّ حِينٍ". قَالَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ: فَوَقَعَ فِي نَفْسِي أَنَّهَا النَّخْلَةُ، وَرَأَيْتُ أَبَا بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ لَا يَتَكَلَّمَانِ، فَكَرِهْتُ أَنْ أَتَكَلَّمَ، فَلَمَّا لَمْ يَقُولُوا شَيْئًا، قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ". فَلَمَّا قُمْنَا قُلْتُ لِعُمَرَ: يَا أَبَتَا، وَاللَّهِ لَقَدْ كَانَ وَقَعَ فِي نَفْسِي أَنَّهَا النَّخْلَةُ. قَالَ: مَا مَنَعَكَ أَنْ تَكَلَّمَ؟ قَالَ: لَمْ أَرَكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ، فَكَرِهْتُ أَنْ أَتَكَلَّمَ أَوْ أَقُولَ شَيْئًا. قَالَ عُمَرُ: لَأَنْ تَكُونَ قُلْتَهَا أَحَبُّ إِلَيَّ مِنْ كَذَا وَكَذَا .

وَقَالَ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا سُفْيَانُ، عَنِ ابْنِ أَبِي نَجِيحٍ، عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ: صَحِبْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ إِلَى الْمَدِينَةِ، فَلَمْ أَسْمَعْهُ يُحَدِّثُ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِلَّا حَدِيثًا وَاحِدًا -قَالَ: كُنَّا عِنْدَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَأَتَى بِجِمَارٍ. فَقَالَ: "مِنَ الشَّجَرِ شَجَرَةٌ مَثَلُهَا مَثَلُ الرَّجُلِ الْمُسْلِمِ". فَأَرَدْتُ أَنْ أَقُولَ: هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ، فَنَظَرَتْ فَإِذَا أَنَا أَصْغَرُ الْقَوْمِ، [فَسَكَتُّ] فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ" أَخْرَجَاهُ .

وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ وَعَبْدُ الْعَزِيزِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ دِينَارٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَوْمًا لِأَصْحَابِهِ: "إِنَّ مِنَ الشَّجَرِ شَجَرَةً لَا يَطْرَحُ وَرَقُهَا، مِثْلُ الْمُؤْمِنِ". قَالَ: فَوَقَعَ النَّاسُ فِي شَجَرِ الْبَوَادِي، وَوَقَعَ فِي قَلْبِي أَنَّهَا النَّخْلَةُ [فَاسْتَحْيَيْتُ، حَتَّى قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ] " أَخْرَجَاهُ أَيْضًا .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي، حَدَّثَنَا مُوسَى بْنُ إِسْمَاعِيلَ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبَانُ -يَعْنِي ابْنَ زَيْدٍ الْعَطَّارَ -حَدَّثَنَا قَتَادَةُ: أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، ذَهَبَ أَهْلُ الدُّثُورِ بِالْأُجُورِ! فَقَالَ: "أَرَأَيْتَ لو عمد إلى متاع الدُّنْيَا، فَرَكَّبَ بَعْضَهَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ أَكَانَ يَبْلُغُ السَّمَاءَ؟ أَفَلَا أُخْبِرَكَ بِعَمَلٍ أَصْلُهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ وَفَرْعُهُ فِي السَّمَاءِ؟ ". قَالَ: مَا هُوَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ: "تَقُولُ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، وَاللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ، وَسُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ، وَالْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ"، عَشْرَ مَرَّاتٍ فِي دُبُرِ كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ، فَذَاكَ أَصْلُهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ وَفَرْعُهُ فِي السَّمَاءِ" .

وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ ﴿كَشَجَرَةٍ طَيِّبَةٍ﴾ قَالَ: هِيَ شَجَرَةٌ فِي الْجَنَّةِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿تُؤْتِي أُكُلَهَا كُلَّ حِينٍ﴾ قِيلَ: غُدوة وعَشيا. وَقِيلَ: كُلَّ شَهْرٍ. وَقِيلَ: كُلَّ شَهْرَيْنِ.

وَقِيلَ: كُلَّ سِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ. وَقِيلَ: كُلَّ سَبْعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ. وَقِيلَ: كُلَّ سَنَةٍ.

وَالظَّاهِرُ مِنَ السِّيَاقِ: أَنَّ الْمُؤْمِنَ مَثَلُهُ كَمَثَلِ شَجَرَةٍ، لَا يَزَالُ يُوجَدُ مِنْهَا ثَمَرٌ فِي كُلِّ وَقْتٍ مِنْ صَيْفٍ أَوْ شِتَاءٍ، أَوْ لَيْلٍ أَوْ نَهَارٍ، كَذَلِكَ الْمُؤْمِنُ لَا يَزَالُ يُرْفَعُ لَهُ عَمَلٌ صَالِحٌ آنَاءَ اللَّيْلِ وَأَطْرَافَ النَّهَارِ فِي كُلِّ وَقْتٍ وَحِينٍ.

﴿بِإِذْنِ رَبِّهَا﴾ أَيْ: كَامِلًا حَسَنًا كَثِيرًا طَيِّبًا، ﴿وَيَضْرِبُ اللَّهُ الأمْثَالَ لِلنَّاسِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَذَكَّرُونَ﴾

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَمَثَلُ كَلِمَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ كَشَجَرَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ﴾ هَذَا مَثَلُ كُفْرِ الْكَافِرِ، لَا أَصْلَ لَهُ وَلَا ثَبَاتَ، وَشُبِّهَ بِشَجَرَةِ الْحَنْظَلِ، وَيُقَالُ لَهَا: "اَلشِّرْيَانُ". [رَوَاهُ شُعْبَةُ، عَنْ مُعَاوِيَةَ بْنِ قُرَّة، عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ: أَنَّهَا شَجَرَةُ الْحَنْظَلِ] .

وَقَالَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ الْبَزَّارُ الْحَافِظُ: حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى بْنُ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ السَّكَنِ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو زَيْدٍ سَعِيدُ بْنُ الرَّبِيعِ، حَدَّثَنَا شُعْبَةُ، عَنْ مُعَاوِيَةَ بْنِ قُرَّةَ، عَنْ أَنَسٍ -أحسَبه رَفَعَهُ-قَالَ: "مَثَلُ كَلِمَةٍ طَيِّبَةٍ كَشَجَرَةٍ طَيِّبَةٍ"، قَالَ: هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ، ﴿وَمَثَلُ كَلِمَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ كَشَجَرَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ﴾ قَالَ: هِيَ الشّرْيان .

ثُمَّ رَوَاهُ عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ الْمُثَنَّى، عَنْ غُنْدَر، عَنْ شُعْبَةَ، عَنْ مُعَاوِيَةَ، عَنْ أَنَسٍ مَوْقُوفًا .

وَقَالَ ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي، حَدَّثَنَا مُوسَى بْنُ إِسْمَاعِيلَ، حَدَّثَنَا حَمَّادٌ -هُوَ ابْنُ سَلَمَةَ -عَنْ شُعَيْبِ بْنِ الحَبْحاب عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ؛ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ: "وَمَثَلُ كَلِمَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ كَشَجَرَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ" هِيَ الْحَنْظَلَةُ". فَأَخْبَرْتُ بِذَلِكَ أَبَا الْعَالِيَةِ فَقَالَ: هَكَذَا كُنَّا نَسْمَعُ.

وَرَوَاهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ حَمَّادِ بْنِ سَلَمَةَ، بِهِ وَرَوَاهُ أَبُو يَعْلَى فِي مسنده بأبسط من هذا فقال: حَدَّثَنَا غَسَّانُ، عَنْ حَمَّادٍ، عَنْ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَنَسٍ؛ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَتَى بِقِنَاعٍ عَلَيْهِ بُسْر، فَقَالَ: وَمَثَلُ كَلِمَةً طَيِّبَةً كَشَجَرَةٍ طَيِّبَةٍ، أَصْلُهَا ثَابِتٌ وَفَرْعُهَا فِي السَّمَاءِ. تُؤْتِي أُكُلَهَا كُلَّ حِينٍ بِإِذْنِ رَبِّهَا فَقَالَ: "هِيَ النَّخْلَةُ" ﴿وَمَثَلُ كَلِمَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ كَشَجَرَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ اجْتُثَّتْ مِنْ فَوْقِ الأرْضِ مَا لَهَا مِنْ قَرَارٍ﴾ قَالَ: "هِيَ الْحَنْظَلُ" قَالَ شُعَيْبٌ: فَأَخْبَرْتُ بِذَلِكَ أَبَا الْعَالِيَةِ فَقَالَ: كَذَلِكَ كُنَّا نَسْمَعُ .

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿اجْتُثَّتْ﴾ أَيِ: اسْتُؤْصِلَتْ ﴿مِنْ فَوْقِ الأرْضِ مَا لَهَا مِنْ قَرَارٍ﴾ أَيْ: لَا أَصْلَ لَهَا وَلَا ثَبَاتَ، كَذَلِكَ الْكُفْرُ لَا أَصْلَ لَهُ وَلَا فَرْعَ، وَلَا يَصْعَدُ لِلْكَافِرِ عَمَلٌ، وَلَا يُتَقَبَّلُ مِنْهُ شَيْءٌ.

---

## 14:27 — verse 27

### Translation

Al-Bukhari said: Abu al-Walid narrated to us, Shu'bah narrated to us, 'Alqamah ibn Marthad informed me, he said: I heard Sa'd ibn 'Ubaydah, from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "The Muslim, when he is questioned in the grave, testifies that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. That is His saying: {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world and in the Hereafter.}"

Muslim also related it, along with the rest of the group, all of them, from the hadith of Shu'bah, with the same chain.

Imam Ahmad said: Abu Mu'awiyah narrated to us, al-A'mash narrated to us, from al-Minhal ibn 'Amr, from Zadhan, from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, who said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ for the funeral of a man from the Ansar. We reached the grave, and it had not yet been given its niche (lahd). The Messenger of Allah ﷺ sat, and we sat around him as though birds were upon our heads. In his hand was a stick with which he was scratching the ground. He raised his head and said: "Seek refuge in Allah from the punishment of the grave," twice or three times. Then he said:

"When the believing servant is in his departure from this world and his approach to the Hereafter, angels descend to him from heaven, white of face, as if their faces were the sun, bringing with them a shroud from the shrouds of Paradise and perfume from the perfume of Paradise, until they sit around him as far as the eye can see. Then the Angel of Death comes and sits at his head, and says: 'O good soul, come out to forgiveness from Allah and His pleasure.'" He said: "So it comes out flowing like a drop flows from the mouth of a waterskin. He takes it, and when he takes it, they do not leave it in his hand for the blink of an eye, but they take it and place it in that shroud and in that perfume. And there comes out from it a fragrance like the finest scent of musk ever found on the face of the earth. They ascend with it, and they do not pass by any assembly of angels without them saying, 'What is this good spirit?' They say: 'So-and-so, son of so-and-so,' using the best names by which he was called in the world, until they bring him to the lowest heaven. They ask for it to be opened for him, and it is opened for him. The angels near to Allah in every heaven accompany him to the heaven that follows, until he is brought to the seventh heaven. Allah says: 'Write the record of My servant in 'Illiyyin, and return him to the earth, for I created them from it, and to it I will return them, and from it I will bring them out again another time.'"

He said: "So his soul is returned into his body, and two angels come to him and make him sit up, and they say to him: 'Who is your Lord?' He says: 'My Lord is Allah.' They say to him: 'What is your religion?' He says: 'My religion is Islam.' They say to him: 'Who is this man who was sent among you?' He says: 'He is the Messenger of Allah.' They say to him: 'What is your knowledge?' He says: 'I read the Book of Allah, so I believed in it and affirmed it as true.' Then a caller calls out from heaven: 'My servant has spoken the truth, so spread out for him bedding from Paradise, and clothe him from Paradise, and open for him a door to Paradise.'" He said: "So there comes to him from its fragrance and its pleasant scent, and his grave is made spacious for him as far as the eye can see. And a man of handsome face, fine clothing, and pleasant scent comes to him and says: 'Rejoice in what pleases you; this is your day which you were promised.' He says to him: 'Who are you? Your face is a face that brings good.' He says: 'I am your righteous deeds.' Then he says: 'My Lord, establish the Hour. My Lord, establish the Hour, so that I may return to my family and my wealth.'"

He said: "And when the disbelieving servant is in his departure from this world and his approach to the Hereafter, angels descend to him from heaven, black of face, bringing with them coarse haircloth garments, and they sit around him as far as the eye can see. Then the Angel of Death comes and sits at his head and says: 'O wicked soul, come out to the wrath of Allah and His anger.'" He said: "So it disperses within his body, and he pulls it out as a many-pronged skewer is pulled out of wet wool. He takes it, and when he takes it, they do not leave it in his hand for the blink of an eye, until they place it in those haircloth garments. And there comes out from it a stench like the foulest smell of a corpse ever found on the face of the earth. They ascend with it, and they do not pass by any assembly of angels without them saying, 'What is this wicked spirit?' They say: 'So-and-so, son of so-and-so,' using the worst names by which he was called in the world, until he is brought to the lowest heaven. It is asked to be opened for him, but it is not opened for him." Then the Messenger of Allah ﷺ recited: {The gates of heaven will not be opened for them, nor will they enter Paradise until a camel passes through the eye of a needle} [al-A'raf: 40]. Allah then says: "Write his record in Sijjin, in the lowest earth." Then he recited: {And whoever associates partners with Allah, it is as though he had fallen from the sky and been snatched by birds, or the wind had carried him down to a far off place} [al-Hajj: 31].

"So his soul is returned into his body, and two angels come to him and make him sit up, and they say to him: 'Who is your Lord?' He says: 'Hah, hah, I do not know.' They say to him: 'What is your religion?' He says: 'Hah, hah, I do not know.' They say to him: 'Who is this man who was sent among you?' He says: 'Hah, hah, I do not know.' Then a caller calls out from heaven: 'He has lied, so spread out for him bedding from the Fire, and open for him a door to the Fire.' So there comes to him from its heat and its scorching wind, and his grave is constricted upon him until his ribs interlock. And a man of ugly face, foul clothing, and putrid smell comes to him and says: 'Receive the news of what will grieve you; this is your day which you were promised.' He says: 'Who are you? Your face is a face that brings evil.' He says: 'I am your wicked deeds.' Then he says: 'My Lord, do not establish the Hour.'"

Abu Dawud related it from the hadith of al-A'mash, and al-Nasa'i and Ibn Majah from the hadith of al-Minhal ibn 'Amr, with the same chain.

Imam Ahmad said: 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated to us, Ma'mar narrated to us, from Yunus ibn Khabbab, from al-Minhal ibn 'Amr, from Zadhan, from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to a funeral, and he mentioned something similar.

In it: "So that when his soul came out, every angel between heaven and earth prayed over him, and every angel in heaven, and the gates of heaven were opened, and there was no group of people at any gate but they were calling upon Allah, Mighty and Majestic, to raise his soul up from among them."

And at its end: "Then there is appointed for him one who is blind, deaf, and mute, having in his hand an iron mallet such that if a mountain were struck with it, it would become dust. He strikes him with a blow so that he becomes dust. Then Allah, Mighty and Majestic, restores him as he was, and strikes him with another blow, so that he cries out with a cry heard by everything except the two weighty ones (jinn and mankind)." Al-Bara' said: Then a door is opened for him to the Fire, and bedding from the Fire is spread out for him.

Sufyan al-Thawri said, from his father, from Khaythamah, from al-Bara', concerning His saying, Exalted is He: {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world}, he said: this refers to the punishment of the grave.

Al-Mas'udi said, from 'Abdullah ibn Mukharriq, from his father, from 'Abdullah, who said: When the believer dies, he is made to sit up in his grave, and it is said to him: "Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your Prophet?" So Allah confirms him, and he says: "My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and my Prophet is Muhammad ﷺ." And 'Abdullah recited: {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world and in the Hereafter.}

Imam 'Abd ibn Humayd, may Allah have mercy on him, said in his Musnad: Yunus ibn Muhammad narrated to us, Shayban ibn 'Abd al-Rahman narrated to us, from Qatadah, Anas ibn Malik narrated to us, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "When the servant is placed in his grave and his companions turn away from him, he indeed hears the sound of their sandals." He said: "Then two angels come to him and make him sit up, and they say to him: 'What did you used to say about this man?'" He said: "As for the believer, he says: 'I testify that he is the servant of Allah and His Messenger.'" He said: "So it is said to him: 'Look at your place in the Fire; Allah has replaced it for you with a place in Paradise.'" The Prophet of Allah ﷺ said: "So he sees them both together." Qatadah said: And it was mentioned to us that his grave is made spacious for him, seventy cubits, and it is filled for him with greenery until the Day of Resurrection.

Muslim related it from 'Abd ibn Humayd, with the same chain, and al-Nasa'i extracted it from the hadith of Yunus ibn Muhammad al-Mu'addib, with the same chain.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Yahya ibn Sa'id, from Ibn Jurayj, Abu al-Zubayr informed me that he asked Jabir ibn Abdullah about the two examiners of the grave, and he said: I heard the Prophet ﷺ say: "This nation is tested in its graves. When the believer is placed in his grave and his companions turn away from him, an angel of severe rebuke comes to him and says to him: What did you used to say about this man? The believer says: I say he is the Messenger of God and His servant. The angel says to him: Look at your seat which was for you in the Fire, God has saved you from it, and has substituted for you, in place of the seat in the Fire that you see, your seat that you see in the Garden. So he sees them both. The believer says: Let me go and give my family the good news. He is told: Be still.

As for the hypocrite, when his family turns away from him, he is made to sit up, and it is said to him: What did you used to say about this man? He says: I do not know, I say what people say. He is told: You neither knew nor did you understand. This is your seat which was for you in the Garden, and it has been replaced in its place with your seat in the Fire."

Jabir said: Then I heard the Prophet ﷺ say: "Every servant is raised in the grave according to the state in which he died: the believer according to his faith, and the hypocrite according to his hypocrisy."

Its chain is sound according to the standard of Muslim, though the two of them (al-Bukhari and Muslim) did not include it.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Abu Amir, Abbad ibn Rashid, from Dawud ibn Abi Hind, from Abu Nadrah, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, who said: We attended a funeral with the Messenger of God ﷺ, and the Messenger of God ﷺ said: "O people, this nation is tested in its graves. When a person is buried and his companions disperse from him, an angel with a mitraq (rod) in his hand comes to him and makes him sit up. He says: What do you say about this man? If he was a believer, he says: I bear witness that there is no god but God, and I bear witness that Muhammad is the servant of God and His Messenger. The angel says to him: You have spoken the truth. Then a door to the Fire is opened for him, and he is told: This would have been your abode had you disbelieved in your Lord, but since you believed, this is your abode. Then a door to the Garden is opened for him, and he wishes to rise toward it, but he is told: Be still. And room is made for him in his grave.

And if he was a disbeliever or a hypocrite, he is told: What do you say about this man? He says: I do not know, I heard people saying something and I said it. He is told: You neither knew nor recited nor were guided. Then a door to the Garden is opened for him, and he is told: This would have been your abode had you believed in your Lord, but since you disbelieved in Him, God, Mighty and Majestic, has substituted this for it. Then a door to the Fire is opened for him, and then he is struck a blow with the rod that is heard by all of God's creation, Mighty and Majestic, except the two weighty kinds (mankind and jinn)."

Some of the people said: O Messenger of God, no one has an angel with a mitraq in his hand standing over him without being terrified at that. The Messenger of God ﷺ said: {God confirms those who believe with a firm word.}

This chain also has no problem in it, for Abbad ibn Rashid al-Tamimi was narrated from by al-Bukhari in conjunction with another narrator, though some scholars weakened him.

Imam Ahmad said: [chain] Husayn ibn Muhammad, from Ibn Abi Dhi'b, from Muhammad ibn Amr ibn Ata', from Sa'id ibn Yasar, from Abu Hurayrah, from the Prophet ﷺ: "The angels attend the dying person. If he was a righteous man, they say: Come out, O tranquil soul, that was in a good body, come out praised, and receive glad tidings of mercy and fragrance and a Lord who is not angry." He said: "This continues to be said to it until it comes out. Then it is taken up to heaven, and the gate is sought to be opened for it, and it is said: Who is this? It is said: So-and-so. They say: Welcome to the good soul that was in the good body, enter praised, and receive glad tidings of mercy and fragrance and a Lord who is not angry." He said: This continues to be said to it until it reaches the heaven in which God, Mighty and Majestic, is.

And if he was an evil man, they say: Come out, O foul soul, that was in a foul body, come out reproached, and receive tidings of scalding water and pus, and other things of its kind, in pairs. This continues to be said to it until it comes out. Then it is taken up to heaven, and the gate is sought to be opened for it, and it is said: Who is this? It is said: So-and-so. It is said: No welcome to the foul soul that was in the foul body, return reproached, for the gates of heaven will not be opened for you. So it is sent down from heaven, and then it goes to the grave. The righteous man sits up and is told the same as was said in the first hadith, and the evil man sits up and is told the same as was said in the first hadith.

Al-Nasa'i and Ibn Majah narrated it, from the route of Ibn Abi Dhi'b, similarly.

In the Sahih of Muslim, from Abu Hurayrah, may God be pleased with him, he said: When the soul of the believing servant comes out, two angels meet it and ascend with it. Hammad said: He mentioned the goodness of its fragrance and mentioned musk. He said: And the people of heaven say: A good soul has come from the direction of the earth, may God's blessing be upon you and upon the body that you used to inhabit. Then it is taken to its Lord, Mighty and Majestic, and He says: Take him to the furthest term.

And as for the disbeliever, when his soul comes out, Hammad said: He mentioned its stench and mentioned wrath, and the people of heaven say: A foul soul has come from the direction of the earth. He said: It is said: Take him to the furthest term. Abu Hurayrah said: The Messenger of God ﷺ then put back a wrap that was on him over his nose, like this.

Ibn Hibban said in his Sahih: [chain] Umar ibn Muhammad al-Hamdani, Zayd ibn Akhzam, Mu'adh ibn Hisham, my father narrated to me, from Qatadah, from Qasamah ibn Zuhayr, from Abu Hurayrah, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "When the believer is taken, the angels of mercy come to him with a white silk cloth and say: Come out to the mercy of God. So it comes out like the most fragrant scent of musk, so much so that they pass it from one to another to smell it, until they bring it to the gate of heaven. They say: What is this good scent that has come from the direction of the earth? And they do not come to any heaven without saying the same, until they bring it to the souls of the believers, who are more joyful over it than a family is over the return of their absent one. They say: What became of so-and-so? They say: Leave him to rest, for he was in distress! He says: He has indeed died, has he not come to you? They say: He was taken to his mother, the Abyss.

As for the disbeliever, the angels of punishment come to him with a sackcloth and say: Come out to the wrath of God. So it comes out like the foulest stench of a corpse, and it is taken to the gate of the earth."

It has also been narrated from the route of Hammam ibn Yahya, from Qatadah, from Abu al-Jawza', from Abu Hurayrah, from the Prophet ﷺ, similarly. He said: "It is asked: What became of so-and-so, what became of so-and-so? What became of such-and-such woman?" He said: "As for the disbeliever, when his soul is taken and brought to the gate of the earth, the keepers of the earth say: We have not found a more foul scent than this. So he is brought down to the lowest earth."

Qatadah said: A man narrated to me, from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, from Abdullah ibn Amr, who said: The souls of the believers are gathered at al-Jabiyah, and the souls of the disbelievers are gathered at Barahut, a salt marsh in Hadramawt.

The hadith master Abu Isa al-Tirmidhi, may God have mercy on him, said: [chain] Yahya ibn Khalaf, Bishr ibn al-Mufaddal, from Abd al-Rahman ibn Ishaq, from Sa'id ibn Abi Sa'id al-Maqburi, from Abu Hurayrah, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ said: "When the dead person, or he said: one of you, is buried, two black, blue-eyed angels come to him, one of them called al-Munkar and the other al-Nakir. They say: What did you used to say about this man? He says what he used to say: He is the servant of God and His Messenger, I bear witness that there is no god but God, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and His Messenger. They say: We already knew that you would say this. Then room is made for him in his grave, seventy cubits by seventy. Then it is illuminated for him, and he is told: Sleep. He says: Let me go back to my family and tell them. They say: Sleep as a bridegroom sleeps, whom none awakens except the dearest of his family to him, until God raises him from that resting place of his.

But if he was a hypocrite, he says: I heard the people saying something, and I said the same as them, I do not know. They say: We already knew that you would say that. Then it is said to the earth: Close in upon him. So it closes in upon him, and his ribs interlock, and he continues to be punished in it until God raises him from that resting place of his."

Al-Tirmidhi then said: This is a hasan gharib (good, singular) hadith.

Hammad ibn Salamah said, from Muhammad ibn Amr, from Abu Salamah, from Abu Hurayrah, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said concerning {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world and in the Hereafter}: "That is when it is said to him in the grave: Who is your Lord? What is your religion? He says: My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, my Prophet is Muhammad. He brought us clear proofs from Allah, so I believed in him and affirmed him as true. Then it is said to him: You have spoken the truth. Upon this you lived, upon this you died, and upon this you will be resurrected."

Ibn Jarir said: Mujahid ibn Musa and al-Hasan ibn Muhammad narrated to us, they said, Yazid narrated to us, Muhammad ibn Amr informed us, from Abu Salamah, from Abu Hurayrah: "Indeed the dead person hears the flapping of their sandals as they turn away departing from him. If he was a believer, the prayer (salah) would be at his head, the zakat at his right, the fasting at his left, and the doing of good deeds, charity, maintaining kinship ties, kindness, and good treatment of people would be at his feet. So he is approached from the direction of his head, and the prayer says: There is no way in through me. He is approached from his right, and the zakat says: There is no way in through me. He is approached from his left, and the fasting says: There is no way in through me. He is approached from the direction of his feet, and the doing of good deeds says: There is no way in through me. Then it is said to him: Sit up.

So he sits up, and the sun appears to him as if it has drawn near to setting. It is said to him: Tell us about what we are going to ask you. He says: Let me pray first. It is said: You will indeed do that, but tell us about what we ask you. He says: What are you asking me about? It is said: What do you say about this man who was among you, and what do you testify concerning him? He says: Muhammad? It is said to him: Yes. He says: I testify that he is the Messenger of Allah, and that he brought us clear proofs from Allah, and we affirmed him as true. It is said to him: Upon that you lived, upon that you died, and upon that you will be resurrected, if Allah wills. Then his grave is expanded for him seventy cubits, and it is illuminated for him, and a door is opened for him to Paradise. It is said to him: Look at what Allah has prepared for you therein. So his joy and delight increase. Then his soul is placed among the good souls, which are green birds that cling to the trees of Paradise, and his body is returned to the earth from which it began." That is the meaning of Allah's words: {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world and in the Hereafter}.

Ibn Hibban narrated it through the route of al-Mu'tamir ibn Sulayman, from Muhammad ibn Amr, and he mentioned the disbeliever's answer and his punishment.

Al-Bazzar said: Sa'id ibn Bahr al-Qaratisi narrated to us, al-Walid ibn al-Qasim narrated to us, Yazid ibn Kaysan narrated to us, from Abu Hazim, from Abu Hurayrah, "I think he attributed it to the Prophet ﷺ," he said: "Indeed when death comes upon the believer and he witnesses what he witnesses, he wishes it, meaning his soul, would come out, for Allah loves to meet him. The believer's soul is raised up to heaven, and the souls of the believers come to him and ask him about their acquaintances among the people of the earth. If he says: I left so-and-so on earth, that pleases them. But if he says: So-and-so has died, they say: He was not brought to us. The believer sits up in his grave and is asked: Who is your Lord? He says: My Lord is Allah. He is asked: Who is your Prophet? He says: Muhammad is my Prophet. It is said to him: What is your religion? He says: My religion is Islam. Then a door is opened for him in his grave, and he says, or it is said to him: Look at your seat. Then he sees the grave, and it is as though it were merely a nap.

As for the enemy of Allah, when death comes upon him and he witnesses what he witnesses, he never wishes for his soul to come out, and Allah hates to meet him. When he sits up, or is made to sit up, in his grave, it is said to him: Who is your Lord? He says: I do not know. It is said: You did not know, then. A door from Hellfire is opened for him. Then he is struck a blow that every creature hears except mankind and jinn. Then it is said to him: Sleep as the one who has been bitten and torn sleeps." I said to Abu Hurayrah: What is "the one who has been bitten and torn"? He said: The one whom beasts and snakes bite and tear. Then his grave is constricted upon him.

Then he [al-Bazzar] said: We do not know of anyone who narrated it except al-Walid ibn al-Qasim.

Imam Ahmad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Hujayn ibn al-Muthanna narrated to us, Abd al-Aziz ibn Abi Salamah al-Majishun narrated to us, from Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir, who said: Asma, meaning the daughter of al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with her, used to relate from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: "When a person enters his grave, if he was a believer, his deeds surround him: the prayer and the fasting." He said: "So the angel comes to him from the direction of the prayer, and it turns him back, and from the direction of the fasting, and it turns him back." He said: "So he calls out to him: Sit up. So he sits up. He says to him: What do you say about this man? Meaning the Prophet ﷺ. He says: Who? He says: Muhammad. He says: I testify that he is the Messenger of Allah. He says to him: How do you know that? Did you meet him? He says: I testify that he is the Messenger of Allah. He says: Upon that you lived, upon that you died, and upon that you will be resurrected.

But if he was wicked or a disbeliever, the angel comes to him with nothing between him and the deeds to turn him back, and he makes him sit up, saying: Sit up. What do you say about this man? He says: Which man? He says: Muhammad? He says: By Allah, I do not know. I heard people saying something, so I said it too. The angel says to him: Upon that you lived, upon that you died, and upon that you will be resurrected." He said: "And a beast is set upon him in his grave, with a whip whose lash is a live coal like the shank of a camel, striking him as much as Allah wills, deaf, not hearing his voice so as to have mercy on him."

Al-Awfi said, from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with both of them, concerning this verse: When the believer's death approaches, the angels witness it, greet him with peace, and give him the glad tidings of Paradise. When he dies, they walk with his funeral procession, then pray over him along with the people. When he is buried, he is made to sit up in his grave and it is said to him: Who is your Lord? He says: My Lord is Allah. It is said to him: Who is your Messenger? He says: Muhammad ﷺ. It is said to him: What is your testimony? He says: I testify that there is no god but Allah, and I testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. So his grave is widened for him as far as his sight can reach.

As for the disbeliever, the angels descend upon him and stretch out their hands, "stretching" meaning striking, they strike his face and his back at death. When he is placed into his grave, he is made to sit up, and it is said to him: Who is your Lord? He gives them no answer at all, for Allah has caused him to forget that mention. When it is said: Who is the messenger who was sent to you? He does not find his way to an answer and gives no reply at all. Thus does Allah lead the wrongdoers astray.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: Ahmad ibn Uthman ibn Hakim al-Awdi narrated to us, Shurayh ibn Maslamah narrated to us, Ibrahim ibn Yusuf narrated to us, from his father, from Abu Ishaq, from Amir ibn Sa'd al-Bajali, from Abu Qatadah al-Ansari, concerning the words of the Almighty {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world and in the Hereafter}, he said: When the believer dies, he is made to sit up in his grave, and it is said to him: Who is your Lord? He says: Allah. It is said to him: Who is your Prophet? He says: Muhammad ibn Abd Allah. This is said to him several times. Then a door to the Fire is opened for him, and it is said to him: Look at your abode in the Fire, had you strayed. Then a door to Paradise is opened for him, and it is said to him: Look at your abode in Paradise, since you remained firm.

As for the disbeliever, when he dies he is made to sit up in his grave, and it is said to him: Who is your Lord? Who is your Prophet? He says: I do not know, I used to hear people saying it. It is said to him: You did not know, then. Then a door to Paradise is opened for him, and it is said to him: Look at your abode had you remained firm. Then a door to the Fire is opened for him, and it is said to him: Look at your abode, since you strayed. That is the meaning of the words of the Almighty: {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world and in the Hereafter}.

Abd al-Razzaq said, from Ma'mar, from Ibn Tawus, from his father, concerning {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world}: he said, this means "there is no god but Allah," and {and in the Hereafter} means the questioning in the grave.

Qatadah said: As for the life of this world, He confirms them through good and righteous deeds, and {in the Hereafter} means in the grave. The same has been related from more than one of the Salaf.

Abu Abdullah al-Hakim al-Tirmidhi said in his book "Nawadir al-Usul": [chain] Abd al-Rahman ibn Samurah said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ came out to us one day while we were in the mosque of Medina, and said: "Last night I saw something wondrous. I saw a man of my ummah [to whom the angel of death had come to take his soul, and his dutifulness to his parents came to him and turned it away. And I saw a man of my ummah] over whom the torment of the grave had been spread out, and his ablution (wudu) came to him and rescued him from that. And I saw a man of my ummah whom the devils had surrounded, and the remembrance of Allah came to him and delivered him from among them. And I saw a man of my ummah whom the angels of torment had surrounded, and his prayer came to him and rescued him from their hands. And I saw a man of my ummah panting with thirst, and every time he came to a pool he was driven away from it, and his fasting came to him and gave him drink and quenched him. And I saw a man of my ummah, while the prophets were sitting in circles, and every time he drew near to any one of them they drove him away, and his ritual bath (ghusl) from major impurity came to him, and took him by the hand and seated him beside me. And I saw a man of my ummah with darkness before him, darkness behind him, darkness on his right, darkness on his left, darkness above him, and darkness below him, and he was bewildered in it, and his Hajj and Umrah came to him and brought him out of the darkness and admitted him into the light. And I saw a man of my ummah speaking to the believers but they would not speak to him, and the tie of kinship (silat al-rahim) came to him and said: O company of believers, speak to him, so they spoke to him. And I saw a man of my ummah shielding his face with his hand from the blaze or sparks of the Fire, and his charity came to him and became a veil over his face and a shade over his head. And I saw a man of my ummah whom the guardians of Hell (al-zabaniyah) had seized from every side, and his enjoining of good and forbidding of evil came to him and rescued him from their hands, and brought him in among the angels of mercy. And I saw a man of my ummah kneeling on his knees, with a veil between him and Allah, and his good character came to him, took him by the hand, and brought him in before Allah, Mighty and Majestic. And I saw a man of my ummah whose record had fallen down toward his left side, and his fear of Allah came to him and took his record and placed it in his right hand. [And I saw a man of my ummah whose scale was light, and his supererogatory deeds (afrat) came to him and made his scale heavy.] And I saw a man of my ummah standing on the edge of Hell, and his dread of Allah came to him and rescued him from that, and he passed on. And I saw a man of my ummah falling into the Fire, and his tears which he had shed from fear of Allah in the world came to him and drew him out of the Fire. [And I saw a man of my ummah standing on the Bridge (al-Sirat), trembling as a palm frond trembles, and his good opinion of Allah came and stilled his trembling, and he passed on.] And I saw a man of my ummah on the Bridge, crawling at times and creeping at times, and his prayer upon me came to him, took him by the hand, raised him up, and he passed on across the Bridge. And I saw a man of my ummah who reached the gates of Paradise, and the gates were closed before him, and the testimony that there is no god but Allah came to him, so it opened the gates for him and admitted him into Paradise."

Al-Qurtubi, after citing this hadith through this chain, said: This is a magnificent hadith. It mentions specific deeds that rescue from specific terrors. He recorded it thus in his book "al-Tadhkirah."

The hafiz Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili narrated concerning this a lengthy gharib (singular) hadith, saying: [chain] from Tamim al-Dari, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "Allah, Mighty and Majestic, says to the angel of death: Go to My close friend (wali) and bring him to Me, for I have tried him with ease and hardship, and I found him where I love him to be. Bring him to Me, that I may give him rest.

So the angel of death sets out to him, accompanied by five hundred angels, with them shrouds and embalming perfume (hanut) from Paradise, and with them bundles of fragrant herbs (rayhan), the stem of the herb being one but at its top twenty colors, each color having a scent distinct from that of its companion, and with them white silk containing pungent musk. The angel of death sits at his head, and the angels surround him closely. Each angel among them places his hand upon one of his limbs, and spreads that white silk and pungent musk beneath his chin, and a door to Paradise is opened for him, so that his soul is soothed at that by a glimpse of Paradise at times, by its spouses at times, by its garments at times, and by its fruits at times, just as a child is soothed by its family when it cries." He said: "And his spouses rejoice greatly at that."

He said: "And the soul leaps." Al-Bursani said: meaning it wishes to hasten from haste toward what it loves. He said: "And the angel of death says: Come out, O good soul, to a lote tree stripped of thorns, and to acacia trees layered with fruit, to shade spread wide, and to water poured forth." He said: "The angel of death is gentler with him than a mother with her child, knowing that this soul is beloved to its Lord, so he seeks by his gentleness to endear himself to it, seeking the Lord's good pleasure toward it, and his soul is drawn out as a hair is drawn out from dough." He said: "Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: {those whom the angels take in death while they are good} [al-Nahl: 32], and He said: {But if he is of those brought near, then rest and fragrance and a garden of bliss} [al-Waqi'ah: 88-89]." He said: "Rest, from the direction of death, and fragrance, with which he is received, and a garden of bliss, which awaits him." He said: "So when the angel of death takes his soul, the soul says to the body: May Allah reward you well on my behalf, for you were swift with me to the obedience of Allah, and slow with me from the disobedience of Allah, so you have been saved and you have brought salvation." He said: "And the body says the like of that to the soul."

He said: "And the tracts of earth in which he used to obey Allah weep for him, and every gate of heaven through which his deeds ascended, and through which his provision descended, weeps for him for forty nights."

He said: "So when the angel of death takes his soul, the five hundred angels remain by his body, and whenever the sons of Adam would turn him onto a side, the angels turn him before them, and they wash him and shroud him with shrouds before the shrouds of the sons of Adam, and with embalming perfume before the embalming perfume of the sons of Adam, and two rows of angels stand from the door of his house to the door of his grave, greeting him with seeking forgiveness. At that Iblis lets out a shriek that nearly shatters the bones of his body." He said: "And he says to his troops: Woe to you! How did this servant escape from you? They say: This was indeed a protected servant."

He said: "So when the angel of death ascends with his soul, Gabriel meets him with seventy thousand angels, each bringing him glad tidings from his Lord distinct from the glad tidings of his companion." He said: "So when the angel of death reaches the Throne with his soul, the soul falls down in prostration." He said: "Allah, Mighty and Majestic, says to the angel of death: Take the soul of My servant and place it in a lote tree stripped of thorns, acacia trees layered with fruit, shade spread wide, and water poured forth."

He said: "So when he is placed in his grave, prayer comes to him and is on his right, fasting comes to him and is on his left, the Qur'an comes to him and is at his head, his walking to the prayer comes to him and is at his feet, and patience comes to him and is to the side of the grave." He said: "So Allah, Mighty and Majestic, sends a company of torment." He said: "It comes to him from his right." He said: "So prayer says: Behind you! By Allah, he never ceased to be diligent with me throughout his life, and he has only now found rest, now that he has been placed in his grave." He said: "So it comes to him from his left, and fasting says the like of that." He said: "Then it comes to him from the direction of his head, and the Qur'an and remembrance say the like of that." He said: "Then it comes to him from the direction of his feet, and his walking to the prayer says the like of that. So the torment does not come to him from any direction seeking to find a way in, except that it finds the close friend of Allah has already taken up his shield." He said: "So the torment is repelled at that and departs." He said: "And patience says to the rest of the deeds: Indeed nothing prevented me from undertaking this myself except that I looked to see what lay with you; had you fallen short, I would have been his defender, but since you have sufficed for him, I remain a reserve for him at the Bridge and the Scale."

He said: "And Allah sends two angels whose sight is like flashing lightning, whose voices are like crashing thunder, whose fangs are like curved horns, and whose breath is like flame, treading upon their own hair, the space between each one's shoulders being a journey of such and such distance. Mercy and compassion have been stripped from them. They are called Munkar and Nakir. In the hand of each of them is a mallet which, if Rabi'ah and Mudar combined their strength upon it, they could not lift."

He said: "So they say to him: Sit up." He said: "So he sits up, sitting fully upright." He said: "And his shrouds fall about his waist." He said: "So they say to him: Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your Prophet?"

He said: They said, "O Messenger of Allah, who could bear to speak at such a moment, given what you describe of the two angels?" He said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: {Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the life of this world and in the Hereafter, and Allah leads the wrongdoers astray, and Allah does what He wills.}

He said: "So he says: My Lord is Allah alone, He has no partner, my religion is Islam, which the angels themselves submit to, and my Prophet is Muhammad, the seal of the prophets." He said: "So they say: You have spoken truly." He said: Then they widen the grave for him, expanding it forty cubits in front of him, forty cubits to his right, forty cubits to his left, forty cubits behind him, forty cubits above his head, and forty cubits at his feet." He said: "So they widen it for him to two hundred cubits."

Al-Bursani said: I think he also said, "and forty cubits," encompassing him.

He said: "Then they say to him: Look above you. And there is a door open to Paradise." He said: "They say to him: O friend of Allah, this is your dwelling, since you obeyed Allah." The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "By the One in Whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, joy reaches his heart at that moment which never departs. Then it is said to him: Look beneath you." He said: "So he looks beneath him, and there is a door open to the Fire." He said: "So they say: O friend of Allah, you have been saved from the last thing that remained upon you." He said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Joy reaches his heart at that moment which never departs." He said: Aisha said: Seventy-seven doors are opened for him to Paradise, from which its breeze and coolness come to him, until Allah, Mighty and Majestic, resurrects him.

And by the aforementioned chain, to the Prophet ﷺ, he said: "Allah, Exalted is He, says to the Angel of Death: Go to My enemy and bring him to Me, for I spread out for him My provision and made easy for him My blessing, yet he refused anything but disobedience to Me. So bring him to Me that I may take vengeance upon him."

He said: "So the Angel of Death goes to him in the most repugnant form that any person has ever seen, having twelve eyes, carrying with him a hooked implement of fire covered with many barbs, accompanied by five hundred angels who carry copper and burning coals from the coals of Hell, and with them whips of fire, soft in texture like ordinary whips, yet being blazing fire." He said: "So the Angel of Death strikes him with that hooked implement a single blow, such that the root of every barb of that implement sinks into the root of every hair, vein, and nail." He said: "Then he twists him with a violent twisting." He said: "Then he draws out his soul from the nails of his feet." He said: "He casts it into his heels, and the enemy of Allah then falls into a stupor from this, and the Angel of Death grants him a brief respite." He said: "And the angels strike his face and his backside with those whips." [He said: "Then the Angel of Death pulls him with a strong pull, drawing his soul out from his heels and casting it into his knees, and the enemy of Allah then falls into a stupor from this, and the Angel of Death grants him a brief respite." He said: "And the angels strike his face and his backside with those whips."] He said: "Then the Angel of Death gives him a wrench, drawing his soul out from his knees and casting it into his waist." He said: "The enemy of Allah then falls into a stupor from this, and the Angel of Death grants him a brief respite." He said: "And the angels strike his face and his backside with those whips." He said: "And so it continues up to his chest, then likewise up to his throat." He said: Then the angels spread out that copper and the coals of Hell beneath his chin." He said: "And the Angel of Death says: Come out, O accursed and cursed soul, to a scorching wind and boiling water, and a shadow of black smoke, neither cool nor pleasant."

He said: "So when the Angel of Death seizes his soul, the soul says to the body: May Allah repay you with evil on my behalf, for you were quick to lead me into disobedience of Allah, and slow to lead me into obedience of Allah. You have perished, and you have caused ruin." He said: "And the body says the same to the soul, and the very tracts of earth on which he used to disobey Allah curse him, and the troops of Iblis rush toward him rejoicing, bringing him the glad tidings that they have brought a servant from among the children of Adam into the Fire."

He said: So when he is placed in his grave, his grave is constricted upon him until his ribs interlock, the right entering into the left and the left into the right." He said: "And Allah sends against him black serpents like the necks of camels, which seize the tip of his nose and the big toes of his feet and gnaw at him until they meet in his midsection."

He said: "And Allah sends two angels whose sight is like flashing lightning, whose voices are like crashing thunder, whose fangs are like curved horns, and whose breath is like flame, treading upon their own hair, the space between the shoulders of each of them being a journey of such and such distance. Mercy and compassion have been stripped from them. They are called Munkar and Nakir. In the hand of each of them is a mallet which, if Rabi'ah and Mudar combined their strength upon it, they could not lift." He said: "So they say to him: Sit up." He said: "So he sits fully upright." He said: "And his shrouds fall about his waist." He said: "So they say to him: Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your Prophet? So he says: I do not know. So they say: You neither knew nor followed guidance." [He said] "So they strike him a blow whose sparks scatter through his grave, then they return." He said: "So they say: Look above you. So he looks, and there is a door open from Paradise. So they say: This, O enemy of Allah, would have been your dwelling had you obeyed Allah."

The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "By the One in Whose hand is my soul, grief reaches his heart at that moment which never departs."

He said: "And they say to him: Look beneath you. So he looks beneath him, and there is a door open to the Fire. So they say: O enemy of Allah, this is your dwelling, since you disobeyed Allah."

The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "By the One in Whose hand is my soul, grief reaches his heart at that moment which never departs."

He said: And Aisha said: Seventy-seven doors are opened for him to the Fire, from which its heat and scorching wind come to him, until Allah sends him into it.

This is a hadith that is extremely gharib (singular), and its narrative sequence is strange. Yazid al-Raqashi, who narrates it from Anas, has gharib and munkar (rejected) reports, and he is weak in transmission according to the scholars. And Allah knows best.

For this reason, Abu Dawud said: [chain] Ibrahim ibn Musa al-Razi told us, Hisham, that is, the son of Yusuf, told us, from Abdullah ibn Bahir, from Hani, the freedman of Uthman, from Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Prophet ﷺ, when he had finished burying a man, would stand over him and say: "Ask forgiveness for your brother, and ask that he be granted steadfastness, for he is being questioned now." Abu Dawud alone transmitted this.

And the Hafiz Abu Bakr ibn Mardawayh cited, regarding the saying of Allah, Exalted is He: {And if you could see when the wrongdoers are in the throes of death, and the angels are stretching out their hands...} [al-An'am: 93], an extremely lengthy hadith, by way of a gharib chain, from al-Dahhak, from Ibn Abbas, as a raised report (marfu'), and it also contains gharib elements.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ الْبُخَارِيُّ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو الْوَلِيدِ، حَدَّثَنَا شُعْبَةُ، أَخْبَرَنِي عَلْقَمَةُ بْنُ مَرْثَد قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ سَعْدَ بْنَ عُبَيْدَةَ، عَنِ الْبَرَاءِ بْنِ عَازِبٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ؛ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "اَلْمُسْلِمُ إِذَا سُئِلَ فِي الْقَبْرِ، شَهِدَ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ، فَذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُ: ﴿يُثَبِّتُ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِالْقَوْلِ الثَّابِتِ فِي الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا وَفِي الآخِرَةِ﴾ .

وَرَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ أَيْضًا وبَقِيَّة الْجَمَاعَةِ كُلُّهُمْ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ شُعْبَةَ، بِهِ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو مُعَاوِيَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا الْأَعْمَشُ، عَنِ المِنْهَال بْنِ عَمْرٍو، عَنْ زَاذَانَ، عَنِ الْبَرَاءِ بْنِ عَازِبٍ قَالَ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ فِي جِنَازَةِ رَجُلٍ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ، فَانْتَهَيْنَا إِلَى الْقَبْرِ وَلَمَّا يُلَحَّدْ، فَجَلَسَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ وَجَلَسْنَا حَوْلَهُ، كَأَنَّ عَلَى رُءُوسِنَا الطَّيْرَ، وَفِي يَدِهِ عُودٌ يَنْكت بِهِ فِي الْأَرْضِ، فَرَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ فَقَالَ: "اسْتَعِيذُوا بِاللَّهِ مِنْ عَذَابِ الْقَبْرِ"، مَرَّتَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثًا، ثُمَّ قَالَ: "إِنَّ الْعَبْدَ الْمُؤْمِنَ إِذَا كَانَ فِي انْقِطَاعٍ مِنَ الدُّنْيَا وَإِقْبَالٍ مِنَ الْآخِرَةِ نَزَلَ إِلَيْهِ مَلَائِكَةٌ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ، بِيضُ الْوُجُوهِ كَأَنَّ وُجُوهَهُمُ الشَّمْسُ، مَعَهُمْ كَفَنٌ مِنْ أَكْفَانِ الْجَنَّةِ وحَنُوط مِنْ حَنُوط الْجَنَّةِ، حَتَّى يَجْلِسُوا مِنْهُ مَدَّ الْبَصَرِ. ثُمَّ يَجِيءُ مَلَكُ الْمَوْتِ حَتَّى يَجْلِسَ عِنْدَ رَأْسِهِ، فَيَقُولُ: أَيَّتُهَا النَّفْسُ الطَّيِّبَةُ، اخْرُجِي إِلَى مَغْفِرَةٍ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَرِضْوَانٍ". قَالَ: "فَتَخْرُجُ تَسِيلُ كَمَا تَسِيلُ الْقَطْرَةُ مِنْ فِي السِّقَاء فَيَأْخُذُهَا، فَإِذَا أَخَذَهَا لَمْ يَدَعُوهَا فِي يَدِهِ طَرْفَةَ عَيْنٍ، حَتَّى يَأْخُذُوهَا فَيَجْعَلُوهَا فِي ذَلِكَ الْكَفَنِ وَفِي ذَلِكَ الحنُوط، وَيَخْرُجَ مِنْهَا كَأَطْيَبِ نَفْحَةِ مِسْكٍ وُجِدَتْ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَرْضِ. فَيَصْعَدُونَ بِهَا، فَلَا يَمُرُّونَ -يَعْنِي بِهَا -على ملأ من الملائكة إِلَّا قَالُوا: مَا هَذَا الرُّوحُ [الطَّيِّبُ] ؟ فَيَقُولُونَ: فَلَانٌ ابْنُ فُلَانٍ، بِأَحْسَنِ أَسْمَائِهِ الَّتِي [كَانُوا] يُسَمُّونَهُ بِهَا فِي الدُّنْيَا، حَتَّى يَنْتَهُوا بِهِ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ الدُّنْيَا، فَيَسْتَفْتِحُونَ لَهُ، فَيُفْتَحُ لَهُ، فَيُشَيِّعُهُ مِنْ كُلِّ سَمَاءٍ مُقَرَّبُوهَا إِلَى السَّمَاءِ الَّتِي تَلِيهَا، حَتَّى يَنْتَهِيَ بِهَا إِلَى السَّمَاءِ السَّابِعَةِ، فَيَقُولُ اللَّهُ: اكْتُبُوا كِتَابَ عَبْدِي فِي عِليين، وَأَعِيدُوهُ إِلَى الْأَرْضِ، فَإِنِّي مِنْهَا خَلَقْتُهُمْ وَفِيهَا أُعِيدُهُمْ، وَمِنْهَا أُخْرِجُهُمْ تَارَةً أُخْرَى".

قَالَ: "فتُعَاد رُوحُهُ [فِي جَسَدِهِ] فَيَأْتِيهِ مَلَكَانِ فَيُجْلِسَانِهِ فَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ: مَنْ رَبُّكَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: رَبِّيَ اللَّهُ. فَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ: مَا دِينُكَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: دِينِي الْإِسْلَامُ. فَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ: مَا هَذَا الرَّجُلُ الَّذِي بُعث فِيكُمْ؟ فَيَقُولُ: هُوَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ. فَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ: وَمَا عِلْمُكَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: قَرَأْتُ كِتَابَ اللَّهِ، فَآمَنْتُ بِهِ وَصَدَّقْتُ. فَيُنَادِي مُنَادٍ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ: أَنْ صَدَقَ عَبْدِي، فَأَفْرِشُوهُ مِنَ الْجَنَّةِ، وَأَلْبِسُوهُ مِنَ الْجَنَّةِ، وَافْتَحُوا لَهُ بَابًا إِلَى الْجَنَّةِ -قَالَ: فَيَأْتِيهِ مِنْ رَوْحِها وَطِيبِهَا، وَيُفْسَحُ لَهُ فِي قَبْرِهِ مَدَّ بَصَرِهِ. وَيَأْتِيهِ رَجُلٌ حَسَنُ الْوَجْهِ، حَسَنُ الثِّيَابِ، طَيِّبُ الرِّيحِ، فَيَقُولُ: أَبْشِرْ بِالَّذِي يَسُرُّكَ، هَذَا يَوْمُكَ الَّذِي كُنْتَ تُوعَدُ. فَيَقُولُ لَهُ مَنْ أَنْتَ؟ فَوَجْهُكَ الْوَجْهُ يَجِيءُ بِالْخَيْرِ. فَيَقُولُ: أَنَا عَمَلُكَ الصَّالِحُ. فَيَقُولُ: رَبِّ أَقِمِ السَّاعَةَ. رَبِّ، أَقِمِ السَّاعَةَ، حَتَّى أَرْجِعَ إِلَى أَهْلِي وَمَالِي".

قَالَ: "وَإِنَّ الْعَبْدَ الْكَافِرَ إِذَا كَانَ فِي انْقِطَاعٍ مِنَ الدُّنْيَا وَإِقْبَالٍ مِنَ الْآخِرَةِ، نَزَلَ إِلَيْهِ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَلَائِكَةٌ سُودُ الْوُجُوهِ، مَعَهُمُ المُسُوح، فَجَلَسُوا مِنْهُ مَدَّ الْبَصَرِ. ثُمَّ يَجِيءُ مَلَكُ الْمَوْتِ حَتَّى يَجْلِسَ عِنْدَ رَأْسِهِ، فَيَقُولُ: أَيَّتُهَا النَّفْسُ الْخَبِيثَةُ، اخْرُجِي إِلَى سَخَط مِنَ اللَّهِ وغَضَب". قَالَ: "فتَفرق فِي جَسَدِهِ، فَيَنْتَزِعُهَا كَمَا يُنْتَزَعُ السَّفُّود مِنَ الصُّوفِ الْمَبْلُولِ، فَيَأْخُذُهَا، فَإِذَا أَخَذَهَا لَمْ يَدَعُوهَا فِي يَدِهِ طَرْفَةَ عَيْنٍ، حَتَّى يَجْعَلُوهَا فِي تِلْكَ الْمُسُوحِ. وَيَخْرُجَ مِنْهَا كَأَنْتَنِ رِيحِ جِيفَةٍ وُجِدَتْ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَرْضِ، فَيَصْعَدُونَ بِهَا فَلَا يَمُرُّونَ بِهَا عَلَى مَلأ مِنَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ إِلَّا قَالُوا: مَا هَذَا الرُّوحُ الْخَبِيثُ؟ فَيَقُولُونَ: فَلَانٌ ابْنُ فُلَانٍ، بِأَقْبَحِ أَسْمَائِهِ الَّتِي كَانَ يُسَمُّونَهُ بِهَا فِي الدُّنْيَا [حَتَّى يَنْتَهِيَ بِهِ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ الدُّنْيَا] فَيُسْتَفْتَحُ لَهُ فَلَا يُفْتَحُ لَهُ". ثُمَّ قَرَأَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: ﴿لَا تُفَتَّحُ لَهُمْ أَبْوَابُ السَّمَاءِ وَلا يَدْخُلُونَ الْجَنَّةَ حَتَّى يَلِجَ الْجَمَلُ فِي سَمِّ الْخِيَاطِ﴾ [الْأَعْرَافِ: ٤٠] ، فَيَقُولُ اللَّهُ: "اكْتُبُوا كِتَابَهُ فِي سِجِّينٍ، فِي الْأَرْضِ السُّفْلَى، فَتُطْرَحَ رُوحُهُ طَرْحًا". ثُمَّ قَرَأَ: ﴿وَمَنْ يُشْرِكْ بِاللَّهِ فَكَأَنَّمَا خَرَّ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ فَتَخْطَفُهُ الطَّيْرُ أَوْ تَهْوِي بِهِ الرِّيحُ فِي مَكَانٍ سَحِيقٍ﴾ [الْحَجِّ: ٣١] .

"فَتُعَادُ رُوحُهُ فِي جَسَدِهِ، وَيَأْتِيهِ مَلَكَانِ فَيُجْلِسَانِهِ وَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ: مَنْ رَبُّكَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: هَاهْ هَاهْ، لَا أَدْرِي. فَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ: مَا دِينُكَ؟ فَيَقُولُ: هَاهْ هَاهْ، لَا أَدْرِي. فَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ: مَا هَذَا الرَّجُلُ الَّذِي بُعِثَ فِيكُمْ؟ فَيَقُولُ: هَاهْ هَاهْ، لَا أَدْرِي. فَيُنَادِي مُنَادٍ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ: أَنْ كَذَبَ فَأَفْرِشُوهُ مِنَ النَّارِ، وَافْتَحُوا لَهُ بَابًا إِلَى النَّارِ. فَيَأْتِيهِ مِنْ حَرِّهَا وَسُمُومِهَا، وَيُضَيَّقُ عَلَيْهِ قَبْرُهُ، حَتَّى تختلف فيه أضلاعه، ويأتيه رجل قَبِيحُ الْوَجْهِ، قَبِيحُ الثِّيَابِ، مُنْتِنُ الرِّيحِ فَيَقُولُ: أَبْشِرْ بِالَّذِي يَسُوءُكَ، هَذَا يَوْمُكَ الَّذِي كُنْتَ تُوعَدُ. فَيَقُولُ: وَمَنْ أَنْتَ فَوَجْهُكَ [الْوَجْهُ] يَجِيئُ بِالشَّرِّ. فَيَقُولُ: أَنَا عَمَلُكَ الْخَبِيثُ، فَيَقُولُ: رَبِّ، لَا تُقِمِ السَّاعَةَ".

وَرَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ مِنْ حَدِيثِ الْأَعْمَشِ، وَالنَّسَائِيُّ وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ مِنْ حَدِيثِ الْمِنْهَالِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، بِهِ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، حَدَّثَنَا مَعْمَر، عَنْ يُونُسَ بْنِ خَبَّابٍ عَنِ المِنْهَال بْنِ عَمْرٍو، عَنْ زَاذَانَ، عَنِ الْبَرَاءِ بْنِ عَازِبٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِلَى جِنَازَةٍ، فَذَكَرَ نَحْوَهُ.

وَفِيهِ: "حَتَّى إِذَا خَرَجَ رُوحُهُ صَلَّى عَلَيْهِ كُلُّ مَلَكٍ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ، [وَكُلُّ مَلَكٍ فِي السَّمَاءِ] وَفُتِحَتْ أَبْوَابُ السَّمَاءِ، لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِ بَابٍ إِلَّا وَهُمْ يَدْعُونَ اللَّهَ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، أَنْ يَعْرُجَ بِرُوحِهِ مَنْ قِبَلِهِمْ".

وَفِي آخِرِهِ: "ثُمَّ يُقَيَّضُ لَهُ أَعْمَى أَصَمُّ أَبْكَمُ، وَفِي يَدِهِ مرزبَّة لَوْ ضُرِبَ بِهَا جَبَلٌ لَكَانَ تُرَابًا، فَيَضْرِبُهُ ضَرْبَةً فَيَصِيرُ تُرَابًا. ثُمَّ يُعِيدُهُ اللَّهُ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، كَمَا كَانَ، فَيَضْرِبُهُ ضَرْبَةً أُخْرَى فَيَصِيحُ صَيْحَةً يَسْمَعُهَا كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا الثَّقَلَيْنِ". قَالَ الْبَرَاءُ: ثُمَّ يُفْتَحُ لَهُ بَابٌ إِلَى النَّارِ، وَيُمَهَّدُ مِنْ فُرُشِ النَّارِ .

وَقَالَ سُفْيَانُ الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ خَيْثَمَة، عَنِ الْبَرَاءِ فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿يُثَبِّتُ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِالْقَوْلِ الثَّابِتِ فِي الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا﴾ قَالَ: عَذَابُ الْقَبْرِ.

وَقَالَ الْمَسْعُودِيُّ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مُخَارق، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: إِنَّ الْمُؤْمِنَ إِذَا مَاتَ أُجْلِسَ فِي قَبْرِهِ، فَيُقَالُ لَهُ: مَنْ رَبُّكَ؟ مَا دِينُكَ؟ مَنْ نَبِيُّكَ؟ فَيُثَبِّتُهُ اللَّهُ، فَيَقُولُ: رَبِّيَ اللَّهُ، وَدِينِيَ الْإِسْلَامُ، وَنَبِيِّيَ مُحَمَّدٌ ﷺ. وَقَرَأَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: ﴿يُثَبِّتُ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِالْقَوْلِ الثَّابِتِ فِي الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا وَفِي الآخِرَةِ﴾ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ عَبَدُ بْنُ حُمَيْدٍ، رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ، فِي مُسْنَدِهِ: حَدَّثَنَا يُونُسُ بْنُ مُحَمَّدٍ، حَدَّثَنَا شَيْبَانُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ، عَنْ قَتَادَةَ، حَدَّثَنَا أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "إِنَّ الْعَبْدَ إِذَا وُضِعَ فِي قَبْرِهِ، وَتَوَلَّى عَنْهُ أَصْحَابُهُ، إِنَّهُ لَيَسْمَعُ قَرْعَ نِعَالِهِمْ". قَالَ: "فَيَأْتِيهِ مَلَكَانِ فَيُقْعِدَانِهِ فَيَقُولَانِ لَهُ: مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِي هَذَا الرَّجُلِ؟ " قَالَ: "فَأَمَّا الْمُؤْمِنُ فَيَقُولُ: أَشْهَدُ أَنَّهُ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ وَرَسُولُهُ". قَالَ: "فَيُقَالُ لَهُ: انْظُرْ إِلَى مَقْعَدِكَ مِنَ النَّارِ، قَدْ أَبْدَلَكَ اللَّهُ بِهِ مَقْعَدًا مِنَ الْجَنَّةِ". قَالَ نَبِيُّ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "فَيَرَاهُمَا جميعا". قال قَتَادَةُ: وَذُكِرَ لَنَا أَنَّهُ يُفْسَحُ لَهُ فِي قَبْرِهِ سَبْعُونَ ذِرَاعًا، وَيُمْلَأُ عَلَيْهِ خَضِرًا إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ.

رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ عَنْ عَبْدِ بْنِ حُمَيْدٍ، بِهِ وَأَخْرَجَهُ النَّسَائِيُّ مِنْ حَدِيثِ يُونُسَ بْنِ مُحَمَّدٍ الْمُؤَدِّبِ، بِهِ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى بْنُ سَعِيدٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ جُرَيْج، أَخْبَرَنِي أَبُو الزُّبَيْرِ، أَنَّهُ سَأَلَ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ عَنْ فَتَّاني الْقَبْرِ فَقَالَ: سَمِعْتُ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ يَقُولُ: "إِنَّ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةَ تُبْتَلَى فِي قُبُورِهَا، فَإِذَا أُدْخِلَ الْمُؤْمِنُ قَبَرَهُ وَتَوَلَّى عَنْهُ أَصْحَابُهُ، جَاءَ مَلَكٌ شَدِيدُ الِانْتِهَارِ، فَيَقُولُ لَهُ: مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِي هَذَا الرَّجُلِ؟ فَيَقُولُ الْمُؤْمِنُ: أَقُولُ: إِنَّهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ وَعَبْدُهُ. فَيَقُولُ لَهُ الْمَلَكُ: انْظُرْ إِلَى مَقْعَدِكَ الَّذِي كَانَ لَكَ فِي النَّارِ، قَدْ أَنْجَاكَ اللَّهُ مِنْهُ، وَأَبْدَلَكَ بِمَقْعَدِكَ الَّذِي تَرَى مِنَ النَّارِ مَقْعَدَكَ الَّذِي تَرَى مِنَ الْجَنَّةِ، فَيَرَاهُمَا كِلَيْهِمَا. فَيَقُولُ الْمُؤْمِنُ: دَعُونِي أُبَشِّرُ أَهْلِي. فَيُقَالُ لَهُ: اسْكُنْ. وَأَمَّا الْمُنَافِقُ فَيُقْعَدُ إِذَا تَوَلَّى عَنْهُ أَهْلُهُ، فَيُقَالُ لَهُ: مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِي هَذَا الرَّجُلِ؟ فَيَقُولُ: لَا أَدْرِي، أَقُولُ كَمَا يَقُولُ النَّاسُ. فَيُقَالُ لَهُ: لَا دَرَيْتَ، هَذَا مَقْعَدُكَ الَّذِي كَانَ لَكَ فِي الْجَنَّةِ، قَدْ أُبْدِلْتَ مَكَانَهُ مَقْعَدَكَ مِنَ النَّارِ".

قَالَ جَابِرٌ: فَسَمِعْتُ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ يَقُولُ: "يُبْعَثُ كُلُّ عَبْدٍ فِي الْقَبْرِ عَلَى مَا مَاتَ، الْمُؤْمِنُ عَلَى إِيمَانِهِ، وَالْمُنَافِقُ عَلَى نِفَاقِهِ".

إِسْنَادُهُ صَحِيحٌ عَلَى شَرْطِ مُسْلِمٍ، وَلَمْ يُخَرِّجَاهُ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو عَامِرٍ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبَّادُ بْنُ رَاشِدٍ، عَنْ دَاوُدَ بْنِ أَبِي هِنْدٍ، عَنْ أَبِي نَضْرَةَ، عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ قَالَ: شَهِدنا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ جِنَازَةً، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ، إِنَّ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةَ تُبتَلى فِي قُبُورِهَا، فَإِذَا الْإِنْسَانُ دُفِنَ وَتَفَرَّقَ عَنْهُ أَصْحَابُهُ، جَاءَهُ مَلِكٌ فِي يَدِهِ مِطْرَاقٌ فَأَقْعَدَهُ، قَالَ: مَا تَقُولُ فِي هَذَا الرَّجُلِ؟ فَإِنْ كَانَ مُؤْمِنًا قَالَ: أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ، وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ وَرَسُولُهُ فَيَقُولُ لَهُ: صَدَقْتَ. ثُمَّ يَفْتَحُ لَهُ بَابًا إِلَى النَّارِ، فَيَقُولُ: هَذَا كَانَ مَنْزِلُكَ لَوْ كَفَرْتَ بِرَبِّكَ، فَأَمَّا إِذْ آمَنْتَ فَهَذَا مَنْزِلُكَ. فَيَفْتَحُ لَهُ بَابًا إِلَى الْجَنَّةِ، فَيُرِيدُ أَنْ يَنْهَضَ إِلَيْهِ، فَيَقُولُ لَهُ: اسْكُنْ. وَيُفْسَحُ لَهُ فِي قَبْرِهِ". "وَإِنْ كَانَ كَافِرًا أَوْ مُنَافِقًا يَقُولُ لَهُ: مَا تَقُولُ فِي هَذَا الرَّجُلِ؟ فَيَقُولُ: لَا أَدْرِي، سَمِعْتُ النَّاسَ يَقُولُونَ شَيْئًا فَيَقُولُ: لَا دَرَيْتَ وَلَا تَلَيْتَ وَلَا اهْتَدَيْتَ. ثُمَّ يَفْتَحُ لَهُ بَابًا إِلَى الْجَنَّةِ، فيقول له: هذا مَنْزِلُكَ لَوْ آمَنْتَ بِرَبِّكَ، فَأَمَّا إِذْ كَفَرْتَ بِهِ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، أَبْدَلَكَ بِهِ هَذَا. فَيُفْتَحُ لَهُ بَابًا إِلَى النَّارِ، ثُمَّ يقمَعه قَمْعَةً بِالْمِطْرَاقِ يَسْمَعُهَا خَلْقُ اللَّهِ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، كُلُّهُمْ غَيْرَ الثَّقَلَيْنِ". فَقَالَ بَعْضُ الْقَوْمِ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، مَا أَحَدٌ يَقُومُ عَلَيْهِ مَلَكٌ فِي يَدِهِ مِطْرَاقٌ إِلَّا هِيلَ عِنْدَ ذَلِكَ. فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: ﴿يُثَبِّتُ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِالْقَوْلِ الثَّابِتِ﴾ .

وَهَذَا أَيْضًا إِسْنَادٌ لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ، فَإِنَّ عَبَّادَ بْنَ رَاشِدٍ التَّمِيمِيَّ رَوَى لَهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ مَقْرُونًا، وَلَكِنْ ضَعَّفَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ.

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا حُسَيْنُ بْنُ مُحَمَّدٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ أَبِي ذِئْبٍ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ عَمْرِو بْنِ عَطَاءٍ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ يَسَار، عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ إِنَّ الْمَيِّتَ تَحْضُرُهُ الْمَلَائِكَةُ، فَإِذَا كَانَ الرَّجُلُ الصَّالِحُ قَالُوا: اخْرُجِي أَيَّتُهَا النَّفْسُ الْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ كَانَتْ فِي الْجَسَدِ الطَّيِّبِ، اخْرُجِي حَمِيدَةً، وَأَبْشِرِي بِرَوْحٍ وَرَيْحَانٍ وَرَبٍّ غَيْرِ غَضْبَانَ". قَالَ: "فَلَا يَزَالُ يُقَالُ لَهَا ذَلِكَ حَتَّى تَخْرُجَ، ثُمَّ يُعْرَج بِهَا إِلَى السَّمَاءِ، فَيُسْتَفْتَحُ لَهَا فَيُقَالُ: مَنْ هَذَا؟ فَيُقَالُ: فَلَانٌ. فَيَقُولُونَ: مَرْحَبًا بِالرُّوحِ الطَّيِّبَةِ كَانَتْ فِي الْجَسَدِ الطَّيِّبِ، ادْخُلِي حَمِيدَةً، وَأَبْشِرِي بِرَوْحٍ وَرَيْحَانٍ، وَرَبٍّ غَيْرِ غَضْبَانَ" قَالَ: فَلَا يَزَالُ يُقَالُ لَهَا ذَلِكَ، حَتَّى يَنْتَهِيَ بِهَا إِلَى السَّمَاءِ الَّتِي فِيهَا اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ.

وَإِذَا كَانَ الرَّجُلُ السُّوءُ قَالُوا: اخْرُجِي أَيَّتُهَا النَّفْسُ الْخَبِيثَةُ كَانَتْ فِي الْجَسَدِ الْخَبِيثِ، اخْرُجِي ذَمِيمَةً، وَأَبْشِرِي بِحَمِيمٍ وغَسَّاق، وَآخَرَ مِنْ شَكْلِهِ أَزْوَاجٍ. فَلَا يَزَالُ يُقَالُ لَهَا ذَلِكَ حَتَّى تَخْرُجَ، ثُمَّ يُعْرَجُ بِهَا إِلَى السَّمَاءِ، فَيُسْتَفْتَحُ لَهَا فَيُقَالُ: مَنْ هَذَا؟ فَيُقَالُ: فَلَانٌ، فَيُقَالُ: لَا مَرْحَبًا بِالنَّفْسِ الْخَبِيثَةِ كَانَتْ فِي الْجَسَدِ الْخَبِيثِ، ارْجِعِي ذَمِيمَةً، فَإِنَّهُ لَا تُفْتَحُ لَكِ أَبْوَابُ السَّمَاءِ. فَيُرْسَلُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ، ثُمَّ يَصِيرُ إِلَى الْقَبْرِ"، فَيَجْلِسُ الرَّجُلُ الصَّالِحُ فَيُقَالُ لَهُ مِثْلَ مَا قِيلَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ الْأَوَّلِ، وَيَجْلِسُ الرَّجُلُ السُّوءُ فَيُقَالُ لَهُ مِثْلَ مَا قِيلَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ الْأَوَّلِ.

وَرَوَاهُ النَّسَائِيُّ وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ، مِنْ طَرِيقِ ابْنِ أَبِي ذِئْبٍ بِنَحْوِهِ .
